it:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"jekyll serve --host=203.0.113.0\"\u003e\u003cpre sure each line in the \u003ccode\u003edescription\u003c/code\u003e is indented at least one space or you’ll run into the error: “could not find expected ’:’ while scanning a simple key at line 19 column 1`.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen you’re done, save and exit your editor. Then, reload the page in your web browser. Depending on your web browser’s local cache settings, you may need to Shfit+Reload to see the changes, which should appear in the two regions highlighted below:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow\" href=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/81d54014832bf1b437901cad00b57560fa22eb1d862fe9ae6da900fd1fa15982/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e6669672d6368616e6765732e706e67\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/81d54014832bf1b437901cad00b57560fa22eb1d862fe9ae6da900fd1fa15982/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e6669672d6368616e6765732e706e67\" alt=\"Screenshot with changes made in the _confg.yml file highlighted\" data-canonical-src=\"http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/config-changes.png\" style=\"max-width: 100%;\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThere are many more customization that can be made in the \u003ccode\u003e_config.yml\u003c/code\u003e file, but for now we’ll move on to the next source file and notice how the changes we made are visible on the rest of the site.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePages: about.md\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-pages-aboutmd\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Pages: about.md\" href=\"#pages-aboutmd\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 dir=\"auto\"\u003eFollow the \u003ccode\u003eAbout\u003c/code\u003e link in the upper-right corner. The changes we made in the configuration file are visible here, above and below the About page’s main content.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow\" href=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/89dc614ca55309e4cc67f00a75c56c5b122742dca7d4e8c781222c75fb2fe517/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f61626f75742e706e67\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/89dc614ca55309e4cc67f00a75c56c5b122742dca7d4e8c781222c75fb2fe517/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f61626f75742e706e67\" alt=\"Screenshot with the about.md content highlighted\" data-canonical-src=\"http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/about.png\" style=\"max-width: 100%;\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThat central content, and the link text in the header, is stored in the \u003ccode\u003eabout.md\u003c/code\u003e file which contains four kinds of content:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e1. Jekyll Front Matter\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nThe block at the top of the \u003ccode\u003eabout.md\u003c/code\u003e file beginning and ending with three dashes is Jekyll’s Front Matter. It must be the first thing in the file, and when it is present, it signals to Jekyll that the file should be parsed. It typically includes valid YAML between the lines to take advantage of pre-defined variables, but it can also be blank. A blank Front Matter block is sometimes useful for a CSS file or other place where you don’t need to set any values but you want access to variables.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \"About” page sets three values in its Front Matter:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"   ---\n   layout: page\n   title: About\n   permalink: /about/\n   ---\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e   ---\n   layout: page\n   title: About\n   permalink: /about/\n   ---\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003eLayout:\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nLayouts eliminate repetitious content like headers, footers, and menus to make sites easier to maintain. Jekyll comes with three layouts: \u003ccode\u003edefault\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003epage\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003epost\u003c/code\u003e. Each one has special characteristics. In this case, a menu link to the title value, “About” appears in the header navigation because the layout is set to “page.”\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003eTitle:\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nIn addition to being used as the link text in the header navigation, the title is also used as the visible page title, formatted with Heading 1 tags, and as the page’s \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;title\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e, which is the text that appears on the browser bar and when the page is bookmarked.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003ePermalink:\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nJekyll automatically generates directories and HTML files from these source files which determine the URL of a page. The permalink allows you to override the default behavior. Here it causes the page URL to be \u003ccode\u003ehttp://203.0.113.0:4000/about/\u003c/code\u003e rather than \u003ccode\u003ehttp://203.0.113.0 :4000/about.html\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e2. Visible Text\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nThe page contents begin after the Front Matter. The text here appears on the page, such as “This is the base Jekyll 3. theme.”\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e3. Markdown\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nMarkdown is a part of the main page contents and controls the format of the content. It will be parsed into HTML for the static site. Markdown is often preferred by content writers over HTML because it is designed to be easier to read and write.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e4. Liquid template directives\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nJekyll uses Liquid as its template engine in order to include dynamic elements. The Liquid directives appear between curly braces such as \u003ccode\u003e{% include icon-github.html username=\"jekyll\" %}\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLet’s make some changes to this page to see how the site is affected.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eChange the Title\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-change-the-title\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Change the Title\" href=\"#change-the-title\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe’ll make a small change and call the page “About me” instead of just “About”:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"nano ~/www/about.md\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003enano ~/www/about.md\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e~/www/about.md\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"---\n. . .\ntitle: \u0026quot;About me\u0026quot;\n. . .\n---\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e---\n. . .\ntitle: \"About me\"\n. . .\n---\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen you’re done, save and exit the file.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe change will appear in three locations, and the menu link will be updated on all the site pages:\u003cbr\u003e\n\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow\" href=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/50893b88c91ac639666fcc021cfe37e266acaccd06aaeb2f4949802b3c517fc8/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f61626f75742d6d652e706e67\"\u003e\u003cimg Page\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-add-a-new-page\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Add a New Page\" href=\"#add-a-new-page\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNext we’ll add a “Contact” page to the site and use a little bit of markdown to include an image.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe’ll start by making an \u003ccode\u003eassets\u003c/code\u003e directory to hold our image:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"mkdir ~/www/assets\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003emkdir ~/www/assets\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThen we’ll transfer the image to our machine using \u003ccode\u003ewget\u003c/code\u003e. The \u003ccode\u003e-O\u003c/code\u003e flag will direct it to the directory we created. The flag requires that we also specify the filename, so we will:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"wget -O ~/www/assets/postcard.jpg http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/postcard.jpg\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ewget -O ~/www/assets/postcard.jpg http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/postcard.jpg\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOnce the image is in place locally, we’ll create the new page:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"nano ~/www/contact.md\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003enano ~/www/contact.md\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e~/www/contact.md\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"---\nlayout: page\ntitle: \u0026quot;Send me a postcard!\u0026quot;\n---\n\nDigitalOcean\\\\\nAttn: Sammy Shark\\\\\n101 Avenue of the Americas\\\\\nNew York, NY 10013\n\n![A postcard](/assets/postcard.jpg)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e---\nlayout: page\ntitle: \"Send me a postcard!\"\n---\n\nDigitalOcean\\\\\nAttn: Sammy Shark\\\\\n101 Avenue of the Americas\\\\\nNew York, NY 10013\n\n![A postcard](/assets/postcard.jpg)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLet’s take a closer look at the markdown. First, the double slash, \u003ccode\u003e\\\\\u003c/code\u003e, at the end of each line forces a return without adding extra space. Second, the image is displayed with this markdown \u003ccode\u003e![]()\u003c/code\u003e. The exclamation mark signals that the link which follows is an image. The brackets contain the alternate text to be used if images are not being loaded or the visitor is using a screen reader. The parentheses contain the link to the image file. You can learn more about Jekyll’s default markdown style on the \u003ca href=\"http://kramdown.gettalong.org/\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ekramdown website\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSave and exit the file, then reload the page. The new link will appear, ordered alphabetically based on the name of the file.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWith the new files in place, the top of our file structure now looks like this:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"├── about.md\n├── assets\n│ └── postcard.jpg\n├── _config.yml\n├── contact.md\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e├── about.md\n├── assets\n│ └── postcard.jpg\n├── _config.yml\n├── contact.md\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe actual webpage page looks likes this:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow\" href=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/2aba6d43253fbb9eed3ee682866e9848a397a78a51adebc384f05a2abeb8784e/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e746163742e706e67\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/2aba6d43253fbb9eed3ee682866e9848a397a78a51adebc384f05a2abeb8784e/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e746163742e706e67\" alt=\"Screenshot of the new Contact page\" data-canonical-src=\"http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/contact.png\" style=\"max-width: 100%;\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eClick the site title to return to the homepage, where you should find the new link included in the header navigation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote:\u003c/strong\u003e It’s common to have an interactive web form on a Contact page. Jekyll \u003ca href=\"https://jekyllrb.com/docs/resources/#integrations\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003edoesn’t provide any built-in form handling\u003c/a\u003e, but you can use cloud-based services such as Disqus, Formspree or FormKeep or host your own.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePosts: _posts/YYYY-MM-DD-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-posts-_postsyyyy-mm-dd-welcome-to-jekyllmarkdown\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Posts: _posts/YYYY-MM-DD-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown\" href=\"#posts-_postsyyyy-mm-dd-welcome-to-jekyllmarkdown\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 provided.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow\" href=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/6346e298ee06050bf256d4fbde4fd993a6d4dd56ccb21219f40e9780449680d7/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f706f7374312e706e67\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://camo.githubusercontent.com/6346e298ee06050bf256d4fbde4fd993a6d4dd56ccb21219f40e9780449680d7/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f706f7374312e706e67\" alt=\"Screenshot of the Welcome to Jekyll post with the main content area highlighted\" data-canonical-src=\"http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/post1.png\" style=\"max-width: 100%;\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003e_posts\u003c/code\u003e directory contains specially named files, following the format \u003ccode\u003eYYYY-MM-DD-Words-in-Title\u003c/code\u003e. If your post is not named in this format, it won’t be parsed. If the file name has a date set in the future, the page will not be parsed for the static site. Naming the file with a future date \u003cem\u003edoes\u003c/em\u003e allow the naming scheme to be used in conjunction with \u003ccode\u003ecron\u003c/code\u003e or other automation strategies to publish a post after particular date and time. The post files can end with \u003ccode\u003e.markdown\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e.md\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e.html\u003c/code\u003e, or other extensions when custom \u003ca href=\"https://jekyllrb.com/docs/plugins/#converters\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003econverters\u003c/a\u003e are installed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003ePosts begin with Front Matter. Front Matter is required for every post file since it contains values like the date that are critical to the creation of the site.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e~/www/_posts/2016-08-31-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"---\nlayout: post\ntitle: \u0026quot;Welcome to Jekyll!\u0026quot;\ndate: 2016-08-31 17:35:19 +0000\ncategories: jekyll update\n---\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e---\nlayout: post\ntitle: \"Welcome to Jekyll!\"\ndate: 2016-08-31 17:35:19 +0000\ncategories: jekyll update\n---\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003eLayout:\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nAlthough it’s possible for a layout to be quite different, the layout for posts is very similar to the default. There are variations in the HTML \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;head\u0026gt; ... \u0026lt;/head\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e section where the page content is different, and the content between the \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;div class=\"wrapper\"\u0026gt; ... \u0026lt;/div\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e tags, but the rest is identical. The only visible difference on the page itself is the automatic inclusion of the the Front Matter’s date value below the title.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003eTitle:\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nThe title appears both as Heading 1 on the blog post itself and as Heading 2 on the index page.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003eDate:\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\nThe date, set here, will determine the date displayed on both the homepage and the post itself. It is this date that will also determine the URL of the post, which we’ll explore in more detail shortly.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote:\u003c/strong\u003e The date in the Front Matter has no direct relationship to the date that begins the filename. The filename must begin with a date in the proper format in order to be parsed at all. If it is named with a date in the future, it won’t be parsed until the next site building process after that date. Meanwhile the Front Matter date determines the directory structure once the file \u003cem\u003eis\u003c/em\u003e parsed and is used as the value displayed on the homepage and the post.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003cem\u003eCategories:\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e Categories are specific to posts and are used to group content by topics. By default, they’re not visible on the page, although they could be added to a custom template.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eRemaining files\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-remaining-files\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Remaining files\" href=\"#remaining-files\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWe’ve looked closely at three files so far, the \u003ccode\u003e_config.yml\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eabout.md\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003e_posts/YYYY-MM-DD-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown\u003c/code\u003e. Here’s a brief overview of the files that are less directly visible from the browser:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003emain.scss\u003c/strong\u003e :\u003cbr\u003e\nJekyll makes use of Syntactically Awesome Style Sheets (Sass), which it compiles into regular CSS each time the site is rebuilt. The .sass files are located in the \u003ccode\u003ecss\u003c/code\u003e directory.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003efeed.xml\u003c/strong\u003e :\u003cbr\u003e\nJekyll provides an RSS feed, also built each time the static site is rebuilt, to allow sites to aggregate posts and provide a way for users to subscribe.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGemfile and Gemfile.lock\u003c/strong\u003e :\u003cbr\u003e\nThe Gemfile lists plugins for Jekyll which are installed with the \u003ccode\u003ebundle\u003c/code\u003e command. When they’re installed, the Gemfile.lock file is generated to track the specific version of the plugins that were installed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOf these four files, only the CSS affects the presentation of the content. If you’re specifically interested in Jekyll and Sass, you can learn more about it from \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/jekyll/jekyll-sass-converter/tree/master/example\"\u003eJekyll’s example site for Sass integration.\u003cbr\u003e\n\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eConclusion\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-conclusion\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Conclusion\" href=\"#conclusion\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn this tutorial, we explored the boilerplate content Jekyll provides when we create a new site and made a few changes to demonstrate how the source files come together on the web pages. This makes a site easier to maintain by setting values in a single place, where they can be updated by a single edit rather than having to change every file. It also allows posts to be dynamically included on the homepage, so you don’t have to worry about manually updating another page to feature a new post.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn \u003ca href=\"/opendocs-md/do-tutorials/blob/master/md/en/controlling-urls-and-links-in-jekyll\"\u003ePart 3\u003c/a\u003e, we’ll look into the file structure of the static site, how that structure is reflected in the URLs of our pages and posts by default, and how to override the default Melissa Anderson","date: 2016-09-21","language: en","license: cc by-nc-sa","source: https://www.digitalocean.com/community/tutorials/exploring-jekyll-s-default-content","---","","# Exploring Jekyll's Default Content","","## Introduction","","Jekyll is a static-site generator that provides some of the benefits of a Content Management System (CMS) while avoiding the performance and security issues introduced by such database-driven sites. It is “blog-aware” with special features to handle date-organized content. Jekyll is well-suited for people who need to work off-line, who prefer to use a lightweight editor instead of web forms for maintaining content, and who wish to use version control to track changes to their website.","","In the [first part](how-to-set-up-a-jekyll-development-site-on-ubuntu-16-04) of this series, we installed Jekyll and its dependencies on an Ubuntu 16.04 server, created a development site in our home directory, and ensured that traffic to the site would be allowed by the firewall.","","In this tutorial, we will use the automatically-generated content from the previous guide to explore how Jekyll turns source files into static content, making it easier to create and maintain content.","","## Prerequisites","","To follow this tutorial, you will need to complete the previous guide, **[How to Set Up a Jekyll Development Site on Ubuntu 16.04](how-to-set-up-a-jekyll-development-site-on-ubuntu-16-04).** We build on the work we did in that tutorial, and without completing it, the examples will not match.","","When you’ve completed Part 1, you’re ready to begin.","","## The Homepage","","Let’s start our exploration on the homepage, which is assembled from four different sources files. We’ll walk through each of those files individually, looking at how they work together to produce the static homepage.","","If you exited the development web server after finishing the first tutorial, restart it again now:","","    cd ~/www","    jekyll serve --host=203.0.113.0","","Then, visit your site in a web browser. The screenshot of the homepage below has been modified to highlight the configuration and information sources.","","![Screenshot of Jekyll Homepage with content labeled by source file](http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/homepage-labeled.png)","","## Configuration Settings: \\_config.yml","","Much of Jekyll’s power comes from the ability to set up information that will be repeated in many places on the static web site in a single source file, `_config.yml`","","The default `_config.yml` created by running `jekyll new`, contains five settings that are visible on the homepage:","","**title:** Your awesome title  ","**email:** [your-e-mail@domain.com](mailto:your-e-mail@domain.com)  ","**description:** Write an awesome description for your new site here …  ","**twitter\\_username:** jekyll  ","**github\\_username:** jekyllrb","","![Screenshot with content provided by the _confg.yml file highlighted](http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/config.png)","","This information is automatically included on all the other pages and posts we create. When we need to update one of these settings, we can make a change in this file, and it will be updated everywhere. To watch this in action, we’ll change these values.","","Open the file in a new terminal:","","    nano ~/www/_config.yml","","We’ll change the settings to the values below:","","    title: Sammy's Blog","    email: sammy@digitalocean.com","    description: \u003e","     Welcome to my blog!","    github_username: DigitalOcean","    twitter_username: DigitalOcean","","We will leave the `url` and `baseurl` alone while we’re developing, and make any adjustments when it’s time to deploy our site.","","To see the changes made in the configuration file, we’ll need to stop the web server with `CTRL-C`, then restart it:","","    jekyll serve --host=203.0.113.0","","**Note:** Be sure each line in the `description` is indented at least one space or you’ll run into the error: “could not find expected ’:’ while scanning a simple key at line 19 column 1`.","","When you’re done, save and exit your editor. Then, reload the page in your web browser. Depending on your web browser’s local cache settings, you may need to Shfit+Reload to see the changes, which should appear in the two regions highlighted below:","","![Screenshot with changes made in the _confg.yml file highlighted](http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/config-changes.png)","","There are many more customization that can be made in the `_config.yml` file, but for now we’ll move on to the next source file and notice how the changes we made are visible on the rest of the site.","","## Pages: about.md","","Follow the `About` link in the upper-right corner. The changes we made in the configuration file are visible here, above and below the About page’s main content.","","![Screenshot with the about.md content highlighted](http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/about.png)","","That central content, and the link text in the header, is stored in the `about.md` file which contains four kinds of content:","","**1. Jekyll Front Matter**  ","The block at the top of the `about.md` file beginning and ending with three dashes is Jekyll’s Front Matter. It must be the first thing in the file, and when it is present, it signals to Jekyll that the file should be parsed. It typically includes valid YAML between the lines to take advantage of pre-defined variables, but it can also be blank. A blank Front Matter block is sometimes useful for a CSS file or other place where you don’t need to set any values but you want access to variables.","","The \"About” page sets three values in its Front Matter:","","       ---","       layout: page","       title: About","       permalink: /about/","       ---","","**_Layout:_**  "," Layouts eliminate repetitious content like headers, footers, and menus to make sites easier to maintain. Jekyll comes with three layouts: `default`, `page`, and `post`. Each one has special characteristics. In this case, a menu link to the title value, “About” appears in the header navigation because the layout is set to “page.”","","**_Title:_**  "," In addition to being used as the link text in the header navigation, the title is also used as the visible page title, formatted with Heading 1 tags, and as the page’s `\u003ctitle\u003e`, which is the text that appears on the browser bar and when the page is bookmarked.","","**_Permalink:_**  "," Jekyll automatically generates directories and HTML files from these source files which determine the URL of a page. The permalink allows you to override the default behavior. Here it causes the page URL to be `http://203.0.113.0:4000/about/` rather than `http://203.0.113.0 :4000/about.html`.","","**2. Visible Text**  "," The page contents begin after the Front Matter. The text here appears on the page, such as “This is the base Jekyll 3. theme.”","","**3. Markdown**  ","Markdown is a part of the main page contents and controls the format of the content. It will be parsed into HTML for the static site. Markdown is often preferred by content writers over HTML because it is designed to be easier to read and write.","","**4. Liquid template directives**  ","Jekyll uses Liquid as its template engine in order to include dynamic elements. The Liquid directives appear between curly braces such as `{% include icon-github.html username=\"jekyll\" %}`.","","Let’s make some changes to this page to see how the site is affected.","","### Change the Title","","We’ll make a small change and call the page “About me” instead of just “About”:","","    nano ~/www/about.md","","~/www/about.md","","    ---","    . . .","    title: \"About me\"","    . . .","    ---","","When you’re done, save and exit the file.","","The change will appear in three locations, and the menu link will be updated on all the site pages:  "," ![Screenshot with the about.md with title changes highlighted](http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/about-me.png)","","### Add a New Page","","Next we’ll add a “Contact” page to the site and use a little bit of markdown to include an image.","","We’ll start by making an `assets` directory to hold our image:","","    mkdir ~/www/assets","","Then we’ll transfer the image to our machine using `wget`. The `-O` flag will direct it to the directory we created. The flag requires that we also specify the filename, so we will:","","    wget -O ~/www/assets/postcard.jpg http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/postcard.jpg","","Once the image is in place locally, we’ll create the new page:","","    nano ~/www/contact.md","","~/www/contact.md","","    ---","    layout: page","    title: \"Send me a postcard!\"","    ---","    ","    DigitalOcean\\\\","    Attn: Sammy Shark\\\\","    101 Avenue of the Americas\\\\","    New York, NY 10013","    ","    ![A postcard](/assets/postcard.jpg)","","Let’s take a closer look at the markdown. First, the double slash, `\\\\`, at the end of each line forces a return without adding extra space. Second, the image is displayed with this markdown `![]()`. The exclamation mark signals that the link which follows is an image. The brackets contain the alternate text to be used if images are not being loaded or the visitor is using a screen reader. The parentheses contain the link to the image file. You can learn more about Jekyll’s default markdown style on the [kramdown website](http://kramdown.gettalong.org/).","","Save and exit the file, then reload the page. The new link will appear, ordered alphabetically based on the name of the file.","","With the new files in place, the top of our file structure now looks like this:","","    ├── about.md","    ├── assets","    │ └── postcard.jpg","    ├── _config.yml","    ├── contact.md","","The actual webpage page looks likes this:","","![Screenshot of the new Contact page](http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/contact.png)","","Click the site title to return to the homepage, where you should find the new link included in the header navigation.","","**Note:** It’s common to have an interactive web form on a Contact page. Jekyll [doesn’t provide any built-in form handling](https://jekyllrb.com/docs/resources/#integrations), but you can use cloud-based services such as Disqus, Formspree or FormKeep or host your own.","","### Posts: \\_posts/YYYY-MM-DD-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown","","Follow the “Welcome to Jekyll” link to take a look at the sample blog post provided.","","![Screenshot of the Welcome to Jekyll post with the main content area highlighted](http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/post1.png)","","The `_posts` directory contains specially named files, following the format `YYYY-MM-DD-Words-in-Title`. If your post is not named in this format, it won’t be parsed. If the file name has a date set in the future, the page will not be parsed for the static site. Naming the file with a future date _does_ allow the naming scheme to be used in conjunction with `cron` or other automation strategies to publish a post after particular date and time. The post files can end with `.markdown`, `.md`, `.html`, or other extensions when custom [converters](https://jekyllrb.com/docs/plugins/#converters) are installed.","","Posts begin with Front Matter. Front Matter is required for every post file since it contains values like the date that are critical to the creation of the site.","","~/www/\\_posts/2016-08-31-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown","","    ---","    layout: post","    title: \"Welcome to Jekyll!\"","    date: 2016-08-31 17:35:19 +0000","    categories: jekyll update","    ---","","**_Layout:_**  ","Although it’s possible for a layout to be quite different, the layout for posts is very similar to the default. There are variations in the HTML `\u003chead\u003e ... \u003c/head\u003e` section where the page content is different, and the content between the `\u003cdiv class=\"wrapper\"\u003e ... \u003c/div\u003e` tags, but the rest is identical. The only visible difference on the page itself is the automatic inclusion of the the Front Matter’s date value below the title.","","**_Title:_**  ","The title appears both as Heading 1 on the blog post itself and as Heading 2 on the index page.","","**_Date:_**  ","The date, set here, will determine the date displayed on both the homepage and the post itself. It is this date that will also determine the URL of the post, which we’ll explore in more detail shortly.","","**Note:** The date in the Front Matter has no direct relationship to the date that begins the filename. The filename must begin with a date in the proper format in order to be parsed at all. If it is named with a date in the future, it won’t be parsed until the next site building process after that date. Meanwhile the Front Matter date determines the directory structure once the file _is_ parsed and is used as the value displayed on the homepage and the post.","","- **_Categories:_** Categories are specific to posts and are used to group content by topics. By default, they’re not visible on the page, although they could be added to a custom template.","","### Remaining files","","We’ve looked closely at three files so far, the `_config.yml`, `about.md`, and `_posts/YYYY-MM-DD-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown`. Here’s a brief overview of the files that are less directly visible from the browser:","","**main.scss** :   ","Jekyll makes use of Syntactically Awesome Style Sheets (Sass), which it compiles into regular CSS each time the site is rebuilt. The .sass files are located in the `css` directory.","","**feed.xml** :   ","Jekyll provides an RSS feed, also built each time the static site is rebuilt, to allow sites to aggregate posts and provide a way for users to subscribe.","","**Gemfile and Gemfile.lock** :   ","The Gemfile lists plugins for Jekyll which are installed with the `bundle` command. When they’re installed, the Gemfile.lock file is generated to track the specific version of the plugins that were installed.","","Of these four files, only the CSS affects the presentation of the content. If you’re specifically interested in Jekyll and Sass, you can learn more about it from [Jekyll’s example site for Sass integration.  ","](https://github.com/jekyll/jekyll-sass-converter/tree/master/example)","","## Conclusion","","In this tutorial, we explored the boilerplate content Jekyll provides when we create a new site and made a few changes to demonstrate how the source files come together on the web pages. This makes a site easier to maintain by setting values in a single place, where they can be updated by a single edit rather than having to change every file. It also allows posts to be dynamically included on the homepage, so you don’t have to worry about manually updating another page to feature a new post.","","In [Part 3](controlling-urls-and-links-in-jekyll), we’ll look into the file structure of the static site, how that structure is reflected in the URLs of our pages and posts by default, and how to override the default <div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h1 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Exploring Jekyll's Default Content</h1><a id="user-content-exploring-jekylls-default-content" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Exploring Jekyll's Default Content" href="#exploring-jekylls-default-content"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Introduction</h2><a id="user-content-introduction" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Introduction" href="#introduction"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Jekyll is a static-site generator that provides some of the benefits of a Content Management System (CMS) while avoiding the performance and security issues introduced by such database-driven sites. It is “blog-aware” with special features to handle date-organized content. Jekyll is well-suited for people who need to work off-line, who prefer to use a lightweight editor instead of web forms for maintaining content, and who wish to use version control to track changes to their website.</p>
<p dir="auto">In the <a href="/opendocs-md/do-tutorials/blob/master/md/en/how-to-set-up-a-jekyll-development-site-on-ubuntu-16-04">first part</a> of this series, we installed Jekyll and its dependencies on an Ubuntu 16.04 server, created a development site in our home directory, and ensured that traffic to the site would be allowed by the firewall.</p>
<p dir="auto">In this tutorial, we will use the automatically-generated content from the previous guide to explore how Jekyll turns source files into static content, making it easier to create and maintain content.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Prerequisites</h2><a id="user-content-prerequisites" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Prerequisites" href="#prerequisites"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To follow this tutorial, you will need to complete the previous guide, <strong><a href="/opendocs-md/do-tutorials/blob/master/md/en/how-to-set-up-a-jekyll-development-site-on-ubuntu-16-04">How to Set Up a Jekyll Development Site on Ubuntu 16.04</a>.</strong> We build on the work we did in that tutorial, and without completing it, the examples will not match.</p>
<p dir="auto">When you’ve completed Part 1, you’re ready to begin.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">The Homepage</h2><a id="user-content-the-homepage" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: The Homepage" href="#the-homepage"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Let’s start our exploration on the homepage, which is assembled from four different sources files. We’ll walk through each of those files individually, looking at how they work together to produce the static homepage.</p>
<p dir="auto">If you exited the development web server after finishing the first tutorial, restart it again now:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="cd ~/www
jekyll serve --host=203.0.113.0"><pre class="notranslate"><code>cd ~/www
jekyll serve --host=203.0.113.0
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Then, visit your site in a web browser. The screenshot of the homepage below has been modified to highlight the configuration and information sources.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/cf9c77c7054e4626c87983f79af90ce4bfb24a1a5bb2d325e24fd645c8cf8ad5/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f686f6d65706167652d6c6162656c65642e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/cf9c77c7054e4626c87983f79af90ce4bfb24a1a5bb2d325e24fd645c8cf8ad5/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f686f6d65706167652d6c6162656c65642e706e67" alt="Screenshot of Jekyll Homepage with content labeled by source file" data-canonical-src="http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/homepage-labeled.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Configuration Settings: _config.yml</h2><a id="user-content-configuration-settings-_configyml" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Configuration Settings: _config.yml" href="#configuration-settings-_configyml"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Much of Jekyll’s power comes from the ability to set up information that will be repeated in many places on the static web site in a single source file, <code>_config.yml</code></p>
<p dir="auto">The default <code>_config.yml</code> created by running <code>jekyll new</code>, contains five settings that are visible on the homepage:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>title:</strong> Your awesome title<br>
<strong>email:</strong> <a href="mailto:your-e-mail@domain.com">your-e-mail@domain.com</a><br>
<strong>description:</strong> Write an awesome description for your new site here …<br>
<strong>twitter_username:</strong> jekyll<br>
<strong>github_username:</strong> jekyllrb</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/4f1192ee0e583c45b1be2af29a80e406f3626cf43caa0f682cb36d67079fd140/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e6669672e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/4f1192ee0e583c45b1be2af29a80e406f3626cf43caa0f682cb36d67079fd140/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e6669672e706e67" alt="Screenshot with content provided by the _confg.yml file highlighted" data-canonical-src="http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/config.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">This information is automatically included on all the other pages and posts we create. When we need to update one of these settings, we can make a change in this file, and it will be updated everywhere. To watch this in action, we’ll change these values.</p>
<p dir="auto">Open the file in a new terminal:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="nano ~/www/_config.yml"><pre class="notranslate"><code>nano ~/www/_config.yml
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">We’ll change the settings to the values below:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="title: Sammy's Blog
email: sammy@digitalocean.com
description: &gt;
 Welcome to my blog!
github_username: DigitalOcean
twitter_username: DigitalOcean"><pre class="notranslate"><code>title: Sammy's Blog
email: sammy@digitalocean.com
description: &gt;
 Welcome to my blog!
github_username: DigitalOcean
twitter_username: DigitalOcean
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">We will leave the <code>url</code> and <code>baseurl</code> alone while we’re developing, and make any adjustments when it’s time to deploy our site.</p>
<p dir="auto">To see the changes made in the configuration file, we’ll need to stop the web server with <code>CTRL-C</code>, then restart it:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="jekyll serve --host=203.0.113.0"><pre class="notranslate"><code>jekyll serve --host=203.0.113.0
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Note:</strong> Be sure each line in the <code>description</code> is indented at least one space or you’ll run into the error: “could not find expected ’:’ while scanning a simple key at line 19 column 1`.</p>
<p dir="auto">When you’re done, save and exit your editor. Then, reload the page in your web browser. Depending on your web browser’s local cache settings, you may need to Shfit+Reload to see the changes, which should appear in the two regions highlighted below:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/81d54014832bf1b437901cad00b57560fa22eb1d862fe9ae6da900fd1fa15982/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e6669672d6368616e6765732e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/81d54014832bf1b437901cad00b57560fa22eb1d862fe9ae6da900fd1fa15982/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e6669672d6368616e6765732e706e67" alt="Screenshot with changes made in the _confg.yml file highlighted" data-canonical-src="http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/config-changes.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">There are many more customization that can be made in the <code>_config.yml</code> file, but for now we’ll move on to the next source file and notice how the changes we made are visible on the rest of the site.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Pages: about.md</h2><a id="user-content-pages-aboutmd" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Pages: about.md" href="#pages-aboutmd"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Follow the <code>About</code> link in the upper-right corner. The changes we made in the configuration file are visible here, above and below the About page’s main content.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/89dc614ca55309e4cc67f00a75c56c5b122742dca7d4e8c781222c75fb2fe517/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f61626f75742e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/89dc614ca55309e4cc67f00a75c56c5b122742dca7d4e8c781222c75fb2fe517/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f61626f75742e706e67" alt="Screenshot with the about.md content highlighted" data-canonical-src="http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/about.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">That central content, and the link text in the header, is stored in the <code>about.md</code> file which contains four kinds of content:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>1. Jekyll Front Matter</strong><br>
The block at the top of the <code>about.md</code> file beginning and ending with three dashes is Jekyll’s Front Matter. It must be the first thing in the file, and when it is present, it signals to Jekyll that the file should be parsed. It typically includes valid YAML between the lines to take advantage of pre-defined variables, but it can also be blank. A blank Front Matter block is sometimes useful for a CSS file or other place where you don’t need to set any values but you want access to variables.</p>
<p dir="auto">The "About” page sets three values in its Front Matter:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="   ---
   layout: page
   title: About
   permalink: /about/
   ---"><pre class="notranslate"><code>   ---
   layout: page
   title: About
   permalink: /about/
   ---
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em>Layout:</em></strong><br>
Layouts eliminate repetitious content like headers, footers, and menus to make sites easier to maintain. Jekyll comes with three layouts: <code>default</code>, <code>page</code>, and <code>post</code>. Each one has special characteristics. In this case, a menu link to the title value, “About” appears in the header navigation because the layout is set to “page.”</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em>Title:</em></strong><br>
In addition to being used as the link text in the header navigation, the title is also used as the visible page title, formatted with Heading 1 tags, and as the page’s <code>&lt;title&gt;</code>, which is the text that appears on the browser bar and when the page is bookmarked.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em>Permalink:</em></strong><br>
Jekyll automatically generates directories and HTML files from these source files which determine the URL of a page. The permalink allows you to override the default behavior. Here it causes the page URL to be <code>http://203.0.113.0:4000/about/</code> rather than <code>http://203.0.113.0 :4000/about.html</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>2. Visible Text</strong><br>
The page contents begin after the Front Matter. The text here appears on the page, such as “This is the base Jekyll 3. theme.”</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>3. Markdown</strong><br>
Markdown is a part of the main page contents and controls the format of the content. It will be parsed into HTML for the static site. Markdown is often preferred by content writers over HTML because it is designed to be easier to read and write.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>4. Liquid template directives</strong><br>
Jekyll uses Liquid as its template engine in order to include dynamic elements. The Liquid directives appear between curly braces such as <code>{% include icon-github.html username="jekyll" %}</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Let’s make some changes to this page to see how the site is affected.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Change the Title</h3><a id="user-content-change-the-title" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Change the Title" href="#change-the-title"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">We’ll make a small change and call the page “About me” instead of just “About”:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="nano ~/www/about.md"><pre class="notranslate"><code>nano ~/www/about.md
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">~/www/about.md</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="---
. . .
title: &quot;About me&quot;
. . .
---"><pre class="notranslate"><code>---
. . .
title: "About me"
. . .
---
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">When you’re done, save and exit the file.</p>
<p dir="auto">The change will appear in three locations, and the menu link will be updated on all the site pages:<br>
<a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/50893b88c91ac639666fcc021cfe37e266acaccd06aaeb2f4949802b3c517fc8/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f61626f75742d6d652e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/50893b88c91ac639666fcc021cfe37e266acaccd06aaeb2f4949802b3c517fc8/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f61626f75742d6d652e706e67" alt="Screenshot with the about.md with title changes highlighted" data-canonical-src="http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/about-me.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Add a New Page</h3><a id="user-content-add-a-new-page" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Add a New Page" href="#add-a-new-page"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Next we’ll add a “Contact” page to the site and use a little bit of markdown to include an image.</p>
<p dir="auto">We’ll start by making an <code>assets</code> directory to hold our image:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mkdir ~/www/assets"><pre class="notranslate"><code>mkdir ~/www/assets
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Then we’ll transfer the image to our machine using <code>wget</code>. The <code>-O</code> flag will direct it to the directory we created. The flag requires that we also specify the filename, so we will:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="wget -O ~/www/assets/postcard.jpg http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/postcard.jpg"><pre class="notranslate"><code>wget -O ~/www/assets/postcard.jpg http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/postcard.jpg
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Once the image is in place locally, we’ll create the new page:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="nano ~/www/contact.md"><pre class="notranslate"><code>nano ~/www/contact.md
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">~/www/contact.md</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="---
layout: page
title: &quot;Send me a postcard!&quot;
---

DigitalOcean\\
Attn: Sammy Shark\\
101 Avenue of the Americas\\
New York, NY 10013

![A postcard](/assets/postcard.jpg)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>---
layout: page
title: "Send me a postcard!"
---

DigitalOcean\\
Attn: Sammy Shark\\
101 Avenue of the Americas\\
New York, NY 10013

![A postcard](/assets/postcard.jpg)
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Let’s take a closer look at the markdown. First, the double slash, <code>\\</code>, at the end of each line forces a return without adding extra space. Second, the image is displayed with this markdown <code>![]()</code>. The exclamation mark signals that the link which follows is an image. The brackets contain the alternate text to be used if images are not being loaded or the visitor is using a screen reader. The parentheses contain the link to the image file. You can learn more about Jekyll’s default markdown style on the <a href="http://kramdown.gettalong.org/" rel="nofollow">kramdown website</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Save and exit the file, then reload the page. The new link will appear, ordered alphabetically based on the name of the file.</p>
<p dir="auto">With the new files in place, the top of our file structure now looks like this:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="├── about.md
├── assets
│ └── postcard.jpg
├── _config.yml
├── contact.md"><pre class="notranslate"><code>├── about.md
├── assets
│ └── postcard.jpg
├── _config.yml
├── contact.md
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The actual webpage page looks likes this:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/2aba6d43253fbb9eed3ee682866e9848a397a78a51adebc384f05a2abeb8784e/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e746163742e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/2aba6d43253fbb9eed3ee682866e9848a397a78a51adebc384f05a2abeb8784e/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f636f6e746163742e706e67" alt="Screenshot of the new Contact page" data-canonical-src="http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/contact.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Click the site title to return to the homepage, where you should find the new link included in the header navigation.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Note:</strong> It’s common to have an interactive web form on a Contact page. Jekyll <a href="https://jekyllrb.com/docs/resources/#integrations" rel="nofollow">doesn’t provide any built-in form handling</a>, but you can use cloud-based services such as Disqus, Formspree or FormKeep or host your own.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Posts: _posts/YYYY-MM-DD-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown</h3><a id="user-content-posts-_postsyyyy-mm-dd-welcome-to-jekyllmarkdown" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Posts: _posts/YYYY-MM-DD-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown" href="#posts-_postsyyyy-mm-dd-welcome-to-jekyllmarkdown"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Follow the “Welcome to Jekyll” link to take a look at the sample blog post provided.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/6346e298ee06050bf256d4fbde4fd993a6d4dd56ccb21219f40e9780449680d7/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f706f7374312e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/6346e298ee06050bf256d4fbde4fd993a6d4dd56ccb21219f40e9780449680d7/687474703a2f2f6173736574732e6469676974616c6f6365616e2e636f6d2f61727469636c65732f6a656b796c6c2d313630342f706f7374312e706e67" alt="Screenshot of the Welcome to Jekyll post with the main content area highlighted" data-canonical-src="http://assets.digitalocean.com/articles/jekyll-1604/post1.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The <code>_posts</code> directory contains specially named files, following the format <code>YYYY-MM-DD-Words-in-Title</code>. If your post is not named in this format, it won’t be parsed. If the file name has a date set in the future, the page will not be parsed for the static site. Naming the file with a future date <em>does</em> allow the naming scheme to be used in conjunction with <code>cron</code> or other automation strategies to publish a post after particular date and time. The post files can end with <code>.markdown</code>, <code>.md</code>, <code>.html</code>, or other extensions when custom <a href="https://jekyllrb.com/docs/plugins/#converters" rel="nofollow">converters</a> are installed.</p>
<p dir="auto">Posts begin with Front Matter. Front Matter is required for every post file since it contains values like the date that are critical to the creation of the site.</p>
<p dir="auto">~/www/_posts/2016-08-31-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="---
layout: post
title: &quot;Welcome to Jekyll!&quot;
date: 2016-08-31 17:35:19 +0000
categories: jekyll update
---"><pre class="notranslate"><code>---
layout: post
title: "Welcome to Jekyll!"
date: 2016-08-31 17:35:19 +0000
categories: jekyll update
---
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em>Layout:</em></strong><br>
Although it’s possible for a layout to be quite different, the layout for posts is very similar to the default. There are variations in the HTML <code>&lt;head&gt; ... &lt;/head&gt;</code> section where the page content is different, and the content between the <code>&lt;div class="wrapper"&gt; ... &lt;/div&gt;</code> tags, but the rest is identical. The only visible difference on the page itself is the automatic inclusion of the the Front Matter’s date value below the title.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em>Title:</em></strong><br>
The title appears both as Heading 1 on the blog post itself and as Heading 2 on the index page.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong><em>Date:</em></strong><br>
The date, set here, will determine the date displayed on both the homepage and the post itself. It is this date that will also determine the URL of the post, which we’ll explore in more detail shortly.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Note:</strong> The date in the Front Matter has no direct relationship to the date that begins the filename. The filename must begin with a date in the proper format in order to be parsed at all. If it is named with a date in the future, it won’t be parsed until the next site building process after that date. Meanwhile the Front Matter date determines the directory structure once the file <em>is</em> parsed and is used as the value displayed on the homepage and the post.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong><em>Categories:</em></strong> Categories are specific to posts and are used to group content by topics. By default, they’re not visible on the page, although they could be added to a custom template.</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Remaining files</h3><a id="user-content-remaining-files" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Remaining files" href="#remaining-files"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">We’ve looked closely at three files so far, the <code>_config.yml</code>, <code>about.md</code>, and <code>_posts/YYYY-MM-DD-welcome-to-jekyll.markdown</code>. Here’s a brief overview of the files that are less directly visible from the browser:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>main.scss</strong> :<br>
Jekyll makes use of Syntactically Awesome Style Sheets (Sass), which it compiles into regular CSS each time the site is rebuilt. The .sass files are located in the <code>css</code> directory.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>feed.xml</strong> :<br>
Jekyll provides an RSS feed, also built each time the static site is rebuilt, to allow sites to aggregate posts and provide a way for users to subscribe.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Gemfile and Gemfile.lock</strong> :<br>
The Gemfile lists plugins for Jekyll which are installed with the <code>bundle</code> command. When they’re installed, the Gemfile.lock file is generated to track the specific version of the plugins that were installed.</p>
<p dir="auto">Of these four files, only the CSS affects the presentation of the content. If you’re specifically interested in Jekyll and Sass, you can learn more about it from <a href="https://github.com/jekyll/jekyll-sass-converter/tree/master/example">Jekyll’s example site for Sass integration.<br>
</a></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Conclusion</h2><a id="user-content-conclusion" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Conclusion" href="#conclusion"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">In this tutorial, we explored the boilerplate content Jekyll provides when we create a new site and made a few changes to demonstrate how the source files come together on the web pages. This makes a site easier to maintain by setting values in a single place, where they can be updated by a single edit rather than having to change every file. It also allows posts to be dynamically included on the homepage, so you don’t have to worry about manually updating another page to feature a new post.</p>
<p dir="auto">In <a href="/opendocs-md/do-tutorials/blob/master/md/en/controlling-urls-and-links-in-jekyll">Part 3</a>, we’ll look into the file structure of the static site, how that structure is reflected in the URLs of our pages and posts by default, and how to override the default behavior.</p>

  </div>

</turbo-frame>

    </main>
  </div>
